 â— AI_MANGER is an InvokeBuild-based PowerShell modular stack for
   centralized CLI tool management and development environment
   automation. It's a sophisticated build/task runner system with
   guards and utilities.

   Key Features:

     - Plugin Architecture: 13 plugins (Audit, Health, Secrets,
   Scanner, Update, Watcher, etc.) for different tooling concerns
     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version
   pinning, and updates
     - Security: DPAPI-based secret vault for API keys/tokens
     - File Scanning: Duplicate detection and misplaced cache/config
   finder
     - Audit Trail: Event 4663 monitoring via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Usage: PowerShell 7 with InvokeBuild module, tasks invoked via
   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

 â— Summary: AI_MANGER vs AIM Comparison

   Yes, AI_MANGER contains useful features NOT in AIM:

   Unique AI_MANGER Features:

     - DPAPI Secrets Vault - Secure Windows user-scoped secret storage
   (API keys, tokens) with clipboard integration - AIM has no secret
   management
     - Health Check System - Environment validation including:
       - Command availability detection
       - PATH order verification
       - Directory existence checks
       - JSON health reports
     - File Scanner - Duplicate file detection by hash + misplaced
   cache/config finder - helps clean up development environments
     - Version Pinning - Enforce exact tool versions across team
   (Pin.Sync/Pin.Report tasks)
     - AuditAlert System - Windows Event 4663 file access monitoring
   via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin - Single PATH wrapper generation (consolidates
   multiple tool PATHs)
     - Watcher Plugin - Real-time file monitoring and change detection
     - Centralized Config - Configuration-driven approach with JSON
   schemas for tools/caches

   What AIM Has (AI_MANGER Lacks):

     - AI tool capability routing (code_generation, refactoring, etc.)
     - Tool fallback chains (if primary fails, try secondary)
     - AI tool audit logging (invocation tracking)
     - Python-based bridge to heterogeneous AI tools

   Recommendation: These are complementary systems. AI_MANGER handles
   environment/secrets/health, while AIM handles AI tool orchestration.
   Consider integrating AI_MANGER's Secrets plugin into AIM for secure
   API key management.

 â— Based on my analysis, here's a strategic integration plan to merge
   AI_MANGER into AIM, creating a unified AI Development Environment
   Manager (AIM+):

   Integration Strategy: AIM + AI_MANGER â†’ AIM+ (Unified AI Dev
   Manager)

   Architecture Vision

     AIM+ (Unified System)
     â”œâ”€â”€ aim/                          # AI Tool Orchestration
   (existing)
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ registry/                 # Tool capability routing
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ adapters/                 # PowerShell bridges
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ bridge.py                 # Python integration
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ environment/              # NEW: From AI_MANGER
     â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ secrets/              # DPAPI vault
     â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ health/               # Environment checks
     â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ installer/            # Tool installation
     â”‚       â””â”€â”€ config/               # Centralized config
     â”œâ”€â”€ config/
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ aim_registry.json         # AI tools (existing)
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ environment.json          # NEW: Merged toolstack config
     â””â”€â”€ scripts/
         â”œâ”€â”€ aim_setup.py              # NEW: Bootstrap everything
         â””â”€â”€ aim_health.py             # NEW: Health checks

   Phase 1: Core Integration (Week 1)

   1.1 Migrate Secrets Management

     - Move AI_MANGER/plugins/Secrets/ â†’ aim/environment/secrets/
     - Create Python wrapper: aim/environment/secrets.py
     - Integration points:  # Before tool invocation, inject secrets
       from aim.environment.secrets import get_secret
       api_key = get_secret("OPENAI_API_KEY")

   1.2 Add Health Check System

     - Move AI_MANGER/plugins/HealthCheck/ â†’ aim/environment/health/
     - Create scripts/aim_health.py:  # Pre-flight check before
   workstream execution
       from aim.environment.health import check_environment
       health = check_environment()
       if not health['ai_tools_available']:
           raise RuntimeError("No AI tools detected")

   1.3 Unified Configuration

     - Merge toolstack.config.json into aim/config/environment.json:  {
         "ai_tools": { /* existing AIM registry */ },
         "environment": {
           "pipx_apps": [...],
           "npm_global": [...],
           "secrets_vault": "%USERPROFILE%/.aim/secrets.json",
           "health_checks": true
         }
       }

   Phase 2: Tool Installation (Week 2)

   2.1 Bootstrap System

     - Create scripts/aim_setup.py (replaces build.ps1):  # One command
    to set up everything
       python scripts/aim_setup.py --install-all
       # - Installs Python tools (aider, ruff, pytest)
       # - Installs Node tools (jules, claude-cli)
       # - Configures secrets vault
       # - Runs health checks
       # - Verifies AI tool detection

   2.2 Version Pinning Integration

     - Add to AIM_registry.json:  {
         "tools": {
           "aider": {
             "pinned_version": "0.5.0",  // NEW
             "auto_update": false         // NEW
           }
         }
       }

   Phase 3: Enhanced Features (Week 3)

   3.1 Scanner Integration

     - Add aim/environment/scanner/:
       - Detect duplicate AI tool installations
       - Find misplaced cache dirs (.aider, .jules, etc.)
       - Consolidate into C:\Tools\cache\aim\

   3.2 Audit Trail Enhancement

     - Extend existing aim/AIM_audit/ with AI_MANGER's AuditAlert:
       - Track AI tool invocations (already exists)
       - Add file access monitoring (from AI_MANGER)
       - Unified JSONL audit log

   3.3 Watcher System (Optional)

     - Add real-time monitoring for config changes:  # Auto-reload AIM
   registry when tools.json changes
       from aim.environment.watcher import watch_config

   Phase 4: PowerShell â†’ Python Migration (Week 4)

   4.1 Rewrite Core Plugins in Python

     - Keep PowerShell adapters for AI tools (they work)
     - Rewrite infrastructure plugins:
       - Secrets â†’ aim/environment/secrets.py (use keyring lib)
       - HealthCheck â†’ aim/environment/health.py
       - Scanner â†’ aim/environment/scanner.py

   4.2 Unified CLI

     # New unified commands
     python -m aim setup          # Bootstrap environment
     python -m aim health         # Check health
     python -m aim secrets set OPENAI_API_KEY
     python -m aim tools list     # Show installed AI tools
     python -m aim tools install aider --pin 0.5.0
     python -m aim scan           # Find duplicates/issues

   Critical Decisions

   1. Keep or Deprecate InvokeBuild?

     - Recommendation: Deprecate. Replace with Python-based task runner
    (Invoke/Nox)
     - Rationale: Main pipeline is Python; reduce language switching

   2. PowerShell vs Python for Secrets?

     - Recommendation: Python (keyring library)
     - Rationale: Cross-platform, better integration with bridge.py

   3. File Structure

     aim/
     â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ bridge.py                  # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ exceptions.py              # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ registry/                  # NEW organization
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ loader.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ validator.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ environment/               # NEW from AI_MANGER
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ secrets.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ health.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ installer.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ scanner.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ adapters/                  # Existing PowerShell scripts
     â””â”€â”€ config/
         â”œâ”€â”€ registry.json          # Merged AI tools + environment
         â””â”€â”€ schema.json

   Migration Path (Low Risk)

   Week 1: Side-by-side (no breaking changes)

     - Copy AI_MANGER features into aim/environment/
     - Keep AI_MANGER working independently
     - Add new scripts/aim_setup.py (optional path)

   Week 2: Soft deprecation

     - Update docs to recommend aim_setup.py
     - Add deprecation warnings to build.ps1

   Week 3: Feature parity validation

     - Run both systems in parallel
     - Verify health checks, secrets, scanning work identically

   Week 4: Sunset AI_MANGER

     - Archive to legacy/AI_MANGER/
     - Update all documentation

   Next Steps

     - Create proof-of-concept: aim/environment/secrets.py (1-2 hours)
     - Design merged config schema: environment.json (1 hour)
     - Prototype aim_setup.py: Bootstrap script (2-3 hours)
     - Test integration: Run workstream with secrets auto-injection (1
   hour)

   Would you like me to start with Step 1 (secrets integration) as a
   proof-of-concept?

 â— AI_MANGER is an InvokeBuild-based PowerShell modular stack for
   centralized CLI tool management and development environment
   automation. It's a sophisticated build/task runner system with
   guards and utilities.

   Key Features:

     - Plugin Architecture: 13 plugins (Audit, Health, Secrets,
   Scanner, Update, Watcher, etc.) for different tooling concerns
     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version
   pinning, and updates
     - Security: DPAPI-based secret vault for API keys/tokens
     - File Scanning: Duplicate detection and misplaced cache/config
   finder
     - Audit Trail: Event 4663 monitoring via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Usage: PowerShell 7 with InvokeBuild module, tasks invoked via
   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

 â— Summary: AI_MANGER vs AIM Comparison

   cache/config finder - helps clean up development environments

   via scheduled tasks

     - Watcher Plugin - Real-time file monitoring and change detection
     - Centralized Config - Configuration-driven approach with JSON
   schemas for tools/caches

   What AIM Has (AI_MANGER Lacks):

     - AI tool capability routing (code_generation, refactoring, etc.)
     - Tool fallback chains (if primary fails, try secondary)
     - AI tool audit logging (invocation tracking)
     - Python-based bridge to heterogeneous AI tools

   Recommendation: These are complementary systems. AI_MANGER handles
   environment/secrets/health, while AIM handles AI tool orchestration.
   Consider integrating AI_MANGER's Secrets plugin into AIM for secure
   API key management.

   Critical Decisions

   1. Keep or Deprecate InvokeBuild?

     - Recommendation: Deprecate. Replace with Python-based task runner
    (Invoke/Nox)
     - Rationale: Main pipeline is Python; reduce language switching

   2. PowerShell vs Python for Secrets?

     - Recommendation: Python (keyring library)
     - Rationale: Cross-platform, better integration with bridge.py

   3. File Structure

     aim/
     â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py

     â””â”€â”€ config/
         â”œâ”€â”€ registry.json          # Merged AI tools + environment
         â””â”€â”€ schema.json

   Migration Path (Low Risk)

   Week 1: Side-by-side (no breaking changes)

     - Copy AI_MANGER features into aim/environment/
     - Keep AI_MANGER working independently
     - Add new scripts/aim_setup.py (optional path)

   Week 2: Soft deprecation

     - Update docs to recommend aim_setup.py
     - Add deprecation warnings to build.ps1

   Week 3: Feature parity validation

     - Run both systems in parallel
     - Verify health checks, secrets, scanning work identically

   Week 4: Sunset AI_MANGER

     - Archive to legacy/AI_MANGER/
     - Update all documentation

   Next Steps

     - Create proof-of-concept: aim/environment/secrets.py (1-2 hours)
     - Design merged config schema: environment.json (1 hour)
     - Prototype aim_setup.py: Bootstrap script (2-3 hours)
     - Test integration: Run workstream with secrets auto-injection (1
   hour)

 â— AI_MANGER is an InvokeBuild-based PowerShell modular stack for
   centralized CLI tool management and development environment
   automation. It's a sophisticated build/task runner system with
   guards and utilities.

   Key Features:

     - Plugin Architecture: 13 plugins (Audit, Health, Secrets,
   Scanner, Update, Watcher, etc.) for different tooling concerns
     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version
   pinning, and updates
     - Security: DPAPI-based secret vault for API keys/tokens
     - File Scanning: Duplicate detection and misplaced cache/config
   finder
     - Audit Trail: Event 4663 monitoring via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Usage: PowerShell 7 with InvokeBuild module, tasks invoked via
   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

 â— Summary: AI_MANGER vs AIM Comparison

   Yes, AI_MANGER contains useful features NOT in AIM:

   Unique AI_MANGER Features:

     - DPAPI Secrets Vault - Secure Windows user-scoped secret storage
   (API keys, tokens) with clipboard integration - AIM has no secret
   management
     - Health Check System - Environment validation including:
       - Command availability detection
       - PATH order verification
       - Directory existence checks
       - JSON health reports
     - File Scanner - Duplicate file detection by hash + misplaced
   cache/config finder - helps clean up development environments
     - Version Pinning - Enforce exact tool versions across team
   (Pin.Sync/Pin.Report tasks)
     - AuditAlert System - Windows Event 4663 file access monitoring
   via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin - Single PATH wrapper generation (consolidates
   multiple tool PATHs)
     - Watcher Plugin - Real-time file monitoring and change detection
     - Centralized Config - Configuration-driven approach with JSON
   schemas for tools/caches

   What AIM Has (AI_MANGER Lacks):

     - AI tool capability routing (code_generation, refactoring, etc.)
     - Tool fallback chains (if primary fails, try secondary)
     - AI tool audit logging (invocation tracking)
     - Python-based bridge to heterogeneous AI tools

   Recommendation: These are complementary systems. AI_MANGER handles
   environment/secrets/health, while AIM handles AI tool orchestration.
   Consider integrating AI_MANGER's Secrets plugin into AIM for secure
   API key management.

   Phase 1: Core Integration (Week 1)

   1.1 Migrate Secrets Management

     - Create Python wrapper: aim/environment/secrets.py

     - Create scripts/aim_health.py:  # Pre-flight check before
   workstream execution

       health = check_environment()
       if not health['ai_tools_available']:
           raise RuntimeError("No AI tools detected")

   1.3 Unified Configuration

         "environment": {
           "pipx_apps": [...],
           "npm_global": [...],

           "health_checks": true
         }
       }

   Phase 2: Tool Installation (Week 2)

   2.1 Bootstrap System

    to set up everything

       # - Installs Node tools (jules, claude-cli)
       # - Configures secrets vault
       # - Runs health checks
       # - Verifies AI tool detection

   2.2 Version Pinning Integration

     - Add to AIM_registry.json:  {

             "auto_update": false         // NEW
           }
         }
       }

     - Add aim/environment/scanner/:
       - Detect duplicate AI tool installations

 â— AI_MANGER is an InvokeBuild-based PowerShell modular stack for
   centralized CLI tool management and development environment
   automation. It's a sophisticated build/task runner system with
   guards and utilities.

   Key Features:

     - Plugin Architecture: 13 plugins (Audit, Health, Secrets,
   Scanner, Update, Watcher, etc.) for different tooling concerns
     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version

     - Audit Trail: Event 4663 monitoring via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Usage: PowerShell 7 with InvokeBuild module, tasks invoked via
   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

   2.2 Version Pinning Integration

     - Add to AIM_registry.json:  {
         "tools": {
           "aider": {
             "pinned_version": "0.5.0",  // NEW
             "auto_update": false         // NEW
           }
         }
       }

   Phase 3: Enhanced Features (Week 3)

   3.1 Scanner Integration

     - Add aim/environment/scanner/:
       - Detect duplicate AI tool installations
       - Find misplaced cache dirs (.aider, .jules, etc.)
       - Consolidate into C:\Tools\cache\aim\

   3.2 Audit Trail Enhancement

     - Extend existing aim/AIM_audit/ with AI_MANGER's AuditAlert:
       - Track AI tool invocations (already exists)
       - Add file access monitoring (from AI_MANGER)
       - Unified JSONL audit log

   3.3 Watcher System (Optional)

     - Add real-time monitoring for config changes:  # Auto-reload AIM
   registry when tools.json changes
       from aim.environment.watcher import watch_config

   Phase 4: PowerShell â†’ Python Migration (Week 4)

   4.1 Rewrite Core Plugins in Python

     - Keep PowerShell adapters for AI tools (they work)
     - Rewrite infrastructure plugins:
       - Secrets â†’ aim/environment/secrets.py (use keyring lib)
       - HealthCheck â†’ aim/environment/health.py
       - Scanner â†’ aim/environment/scanner.py

   4.2 Unified CLI

     # New unified commands
     python -m aim setup          # Bootstrap environment
     python -m aim health         # Check health
     python -m aim secrets set OPENAI_API_KEY
     python -m aim tools list     # Show installed AI tools
     python -m aim tools install aider --pin 0.5.0
     python -m aim scan           # Find duplicates/issues

   Critical Decisions

   1. Keep or Deprecate InvokeBuild?

     - Recommendation: Deprecate. Replace with Python-based task runner
    (Invoke/Nox)
     - Rationale: Main pipeline is Python; reduce language switching

   2. PowerShell vs Python for Secrets?

     - Recommendation: Python (keyring library)
     - Rationale: Cross-platform, better integration with bridge.py

   3. File Structure

     aim/
     â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ bridge.py                  # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ exceptions.py              # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ registry/                  # NEW organization
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ loader.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ validator.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ environment/               # NEW from AI_MANGER
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ secrets.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ health.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ installer.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ scanner.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ adapters/                  # Existing PowerShell scripts
     â””â”€â”€ config/
         â”œâ”€â”€ registry.json          # Merged AI tools + environment
         â””â”€â”€ schema.json

   Migration Path (Low Risk)

   Week 1: Side-by-side (no breaking changes)

     - Copy AI_MANGER features into aim/environment/
     - Keep AI_MANGER working independently
     - Add new scripts/aim_setup.py (optional path)

   Week 2: Soft deprecation

     - Update docs to recommend aim_setup.py
     - Add deprecation warnings to build.ps1

   Week 3: Feature parity validation

     - Run both systems in parallel
     - Verify health checks, secrets, scanning work identically

   Week 4: Sunset AI_MANGER

     - Archive to legacy/AI_MANGER/
     - Update all documentation

   Next Steps

     - Create proof-of-concept: aim/environment/secrets.py (1-2 hours)
     - Design merged config schema: environment.json (1 hour)
     - Prototype aim_setup.py: Bootstrap script (2-3 hours)
     - Test integration: Run workstream with secrets auto-injection (1
   hour)

   Would you like me to start with Step 1 (secrets integration) as a
   proof-of-concept?

 â— AI_MANGER is an InvokeBuild-based PowerShell modular stack for
   centralized CLI tool management and development environment
   automation. It's a sophisticated build/task runner system with
   guards and utilities.

   Key Features:

     - Plugin Architecture: 13 plugins (Audit, Health, Secrets,
   Scanner, Update, Watcher, etc.) for different tooling concerns
     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version
   pinning, and updates
     - Security: DPAPI-based secret vault for API keys/tokens
     - File Scanning: Duplicate detection and misplaced cache/config
   finder
     - Audit Trail: Event 4663 monitoring via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Usage: PowerShell 7 with InvokeBuild module, tasks invoked via
   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

 â— Summary: AI_MANGER vs AIM Comparison

   Yes, AI_MANGER contains useful features NOT in AIM:

   Unique AI_MANGER Features:

     - DPAPI Secrets Vault - Secure Windows user-scoped secret storage
   (API keys, tokens) with clipboard integration - AIM has no secret
   management
     - Health Check System - Environment validation including:
       - Command availability detection
       - PATH order verification
       - Directory existence checks
       - JSON health reports
     - File Scanner - Duplicate file detection by hash + misplaced
   cache/config finder - helps clean up development environments
     - Version Pinning - Enforce exact tool versions across team
   (Pin.Sync/Pin.Report tasks)
     - AuditAlert System - Windows Event 4663 file access monitoring
   via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin - Single PATH wrapper generation (consolidates
   multiple tool PATHs)
     - Watcher Plugin - Real-time file monitoring and change detection
     - Centralized Config - Configuration-driven approach with JSON
   schemas for tools/caches

   What AIM Has (AI_MANGER Lacks):

     - AI tool capability routing (code_generation, refactoring, etc.)
     - Tool fallback chains (if primary fails, try secondary)
     - AI tool audit logging (invocation tracking)
     - Python-based bridge to heterogeneous AI tools

   Recommendation: These are complementary systems. AI_MANGER handles
   environment/secrets/health, while AIM handles AI tool orchestration.
   Consider integrating AI_MANGER's Secrets plugin into AIM for secure
   API key management.

   Phase 1: Core Integration (Week 1)

     - Create Python wrapper: aim/environment/secrets.py

           raise RuntimeError("No AI tools detected")

     - Rationale: Cross-platform, better integration with bridge.py

   centralized CLI tool management and development environment

     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version

     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

   (API keys, tokens) with clipboard integration - AIM has no secret
   management
     - Health Check System - Environment validation including:
       - Command availability detection
       - PATH order verification
       - Directory existence checks
       - JSON health reports
     - File Scanner - Duplicate file detection by hash + misplaced
   cache/config finder - helps clean up development environments
     - Version Pinning - Enforce exact tool versions across team
   (Pin.Sync/Pin.Report tasks)
     - AuditAlert System - Windows Event 4663 file access monitoring
   via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin - Single PATH wrapper generation (consolidates
   multiple tool PATHs)
     - Watcher Plugin - Real-time file monitoring and change detection
     - Centralized Config - Configuration-driven approach with JSON
   schemas for tools/caches

   What AIM Has (AI_MANGER Lacks):

     - AI tool capability routing (code_generation, refactoring, etc.)
     - Tool fallback chains (if primary fails, try secondary)
     - AI tool audit logging (invocation tracking)
     - Python-based bridge to heterogeneous AI tools

   Recommendation: These are complementary systems. AI_MANGER handles
   environment/secrets/health, while AIM handles AI tool orchestration.
   Consider integrating AI_MANGER's Secrets plugin into AIM for secure
   API key management.

 â— Based on my analysis, here's a strategic integration plan to merge
   AI_MANGER into AIM, creating a unified AI Development Environment
   Manager (AIM+):

   Integration Strategy: AIM + AI_MANGER â†’ AIM+ (Unified AI Dev
   Manager)

   Architecture Vision

     AIM+ (Unified System)
     â”œâ”€â”€ aim/                          # AI Tool Orchestration
   (existing)
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ registry/                 # Tool capability routing
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ adapters/                 # PowerShell bridges
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ bridge.py                 # Python integration
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ environment/              # NEW: From AI_MANGER
     â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ secrets/              # DPAPI vault
     â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ health/               # Environment checks
     â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ installer/            # Tool installation
     â”‚       â””â”€â”€ config/               # Centralized config
     â”œâ”€â”€ config/
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ aim_registry.json         # AI tools (existing)
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ environment.json          # NEW: Merged toolstack config
     â””â”€â”€ scripts/
         â”œâ”€â”€ aim_setup.py              # NEW: Bootstrap everything
         â””â”€â”€ aim_health.py             # NEW: Health checks

   Phase 1: Core Integration (Week 1)

   1.1 Migrate Secrets Management

     - Move AI_MANGER/plugins/Secrets/ â†’ aim/environment/secrets/
     - Create Python wrapper: aim/environment/secrets.py
     - Integration points:  # Before tool invocation, inject secrets
       from aim.environment.secrets import get_secret
       api_key = get_secret("OPENAI_API_KEY")

   1.2 Add Health Check System

     - Move AI_MANGER/plugins/HealthCheck/ â†’ aim/environment/health/
     - Create scripts/aim_health.py:  # Pre-flight check before
   workstream execution
       from aim.environment.health import check_environment
       health = check_environment()
       if not health['ai_tools_available']:
           raise RuntimeError("No AI tools detected")

   1.3 Unified Configuration

     - Merge toolstack.config.json into aim/config/environment.json:  {
         "ai_tools": { /* existing AIM registry */ },
         "environment": {
           "pipx_apps": [...],
           "npm_global": [...],
           "secrets_vault": "%USERPROFILE%/.aim/secrets.json",
           "health_checks": true
         }
       }

   Phase 2: Tool Installation (Week 2)

   2.1 Bootstrap System

     - Create scripts/aim_setup.py (replaces build.ps1):  # One command
    to set up everything
       python scripts/aim_setup.py --install-all
       # - Installs Python tools (aider, ruff, pytest)
       # - Installs Node tools (jules, claude-cli)
       # - Configures secrets vault
       # - Runs health checks
       # - Verifies AI tool detection

   2.2 Version Pinning Integration

     - Add to AIM_registry.json:  {
         "tools": {
           "aider": {
             "pinned_version": "0.5.0",  // NEW
             "auto_update": false         // NEW
           }
         }
       }

   Phase 3: Enhanced Features (Week 3)

   3.1 Scanner Integration

     - Add aim/environment/scanner/:
       - Detect duplicate AI tool installations
       - Find misplaced cache dirs (.aider, .jules, etc.)
       - Consolidate into C:\Tools\cache\aim\

   3.2 Audit Trail Enhancement

     - Extend existing aim/AIM_audit/ with AI_MANGER's AuditAlert:
       - Track AI tool invocations (already exists)
       - Add file access monitoring (from AI_MANGER)
       - Unified JSONL audit log

   3.3 Watcher System (Optional)

     - Add real-time monitoring for config changes:  # Auto-reload AIM
   registry when tools.json changes
       from aim.environment.watcher import watch_config

   Phase 4: PowerShell â†’ Python Migration (Week 4)

   4.1 Rewrite Core Plugins in Python

     - Keep PowerShell adapters for AI tools (they work)
     - Rewrite infrastructure plugins:
       - Secrets â†’ aim/environment/secrets.py (use keyring lib)
       - HealthCheck â†’ aim/environment/health.py
       - Scanner â†’ aim/environment/scanner.py

   4.2 Unified CLI

     # New unified commands
     python -m aim setup          # Bootstrap environment
     python -m aim health         # Check health
     python -m aim secrets set OPENAI_API_KEY
     python -m aim tools list     # Show installed AI tools
     python -m aim tools install aider --pin 0.5.0
     python -m aim scan           # Find duplicates/issues

   Critical Decisions

   1. Keep or Deprecate InvokeBuild?

     - Recommendation: Deprecate. Replace with Python-based task runner
    (Invoke/Nox)
     - Rationale: Main pipeline is Python; reduce language switching

   2. PowerShell vs Python for Secrets?

     - Recommendation: Python (keyring library)
     - Rationale: Cross-platform, better integration with bridge.py

   3. File Structure

     aim/
     â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ bridge.py                  # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ exceptions.py              # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ registry/                  # NEW organization
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ loader.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ validator.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ environment/               # NEW from AI_MANGER
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ secrets.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ health.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ installer.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ scanner.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ adapters/                  # Existing PowerShell scripts
     â””â”€â”€ config/
         â”œâ”€â”€ registry.json          # Merged AI tools + environment
         â””â”€â”€ schema.json

   Migration Path (Low Risk)

   Week 1: Side-by-side (no breaking changes)

     - Copy AI_MANGER features into aim/environment/
     - Keep AI_MANGER working independently
     - Add new scripts/aim_setup.py (optional path)

   Week 2: Soft deprecation

     - Update docs to recommend aim_setup.py
     - Add deprecation warnings to build.ps1

   Week 3: Feature parity validation

     - Run both systems in parallel
     - Verify health checks, secrets, scanning work identically

   Week 4: Sunset AI_MANGER

     - Archive to legacy/AI_MANGER/
     - Update all documentation

   Next Steps

     - Create proof-of-concept: aim/environment/secrets.py (1-2 hours)
     - Design merged config schema: environment.json (1 hour)
     - Prototype aim_setup.py: Bootstrap script (2-3 hours)
     - Test integration: Run workstream with secrets auto-injection (1
   hour)

 â— AI_MANGER is an InvokeBuild-based PowerShell modular stack for
   centralized CLI tool management and development environment
   automation. It's a sophisticated build/task runner system with
   guards and utilities.

   Key Features:

     - Plugin Architecture: 13 plugins (Audit, Health, Secrets,
   Scanner, Update, Watcher, etc.) for different tooling concerns
     - CLI Management: Handles npm/pipx tool installations, version
   pinning, and updates
     - Security: DPAPI-based secret vault for API keys/tokens
     - File Scanning: Duplicate detection and misplaced cache/config
   finder
     - Audit Trail: Event 4663 monitoring via scheduled tasks
     - MasterBin: Single PATH wrapper generation for tools
     - Health Checks: Environment validation and reporting

   Usage: PowerShell 7 with InvokeBuild module, tasks invoked via
   Invoke-Build -File .\build.ps1 <TaskName>, configurable via JSON in
   config/.

   This appears to be a developer productivity/environment management
   system separate from but potentially complementary to the
   AGENTIC_DEV_PROTOTYPE pipeline project.

     - AI tool audit logging (invocation tracking)
     - Python-based bridge to heterogeneous AI tools

   Recommendation: These are complementary systems. AI_MANGER handles
   environment/secrets/health, while AIM handles AI tool orchestration.
   Consider integrating AI_MANGER's Secrets plugin into AIM for secure
   API key management.

   Critical Decisions

   1. Keep or Deprecate InvokeBuild?

     - Recommendation: Deprecate. Replace with Python-based task runner
    (Invoke/Nox)
     - Rationale: Main pipeline is Python; reduce language switching

   2. PowerShell vs Python for Secrets?

     - Recommendation: Python (keyring library)
     - Rationale: Cross-platform, better integration with bridge.py

   3. File Structure

     aim/
     â”œâ”€â”€ __init__.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ bridge.py                  # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ exceptions.py              # Existing
     â”œâ”€â”€ registry/                  # NEW organization
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ loader.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ validator.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ environment/               # NEW from AI_MANGER
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ secrets.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ health.py
     â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ installer.py
     â”‚   â””â”€â”€ scanner.py
     â”œâ”€â”€ adapters/                  # Existing PowerShell scripts
     â””â”€â”€ config/
         â”œâ”€â”€ registry.json          # Merged AI tools + environment
         â””â”€â”€ schema.json

   Migration Path (Low Risk)

   Week 1: Side-by-side (no breaking changes)

     - Copy AI_MANGER features into aim/environment/
     - Keep AI_MANGER working independently
     - Add new scripts/aim_setup.py (optional path)

   Week 2: Soft deprecation

     - Update docs to recommend aim_setup.py
     - Add deprecation warnings to build.ps1

   Week 3: Feature parity validation

     - Run both systems in parallel
     - Verify health checks, secrets, scanning work identically

   Week 4: Sunset AI_MANGER

     - Archive to legacy/AI_MANGER/
     - Update all documentation

   Next Steps

     - Create proof-of-concept: aim/environment/secrets.py (1-2 hours)
     - Design merged config schema: environment.json (1 hour)
     - Prototype aim_setup.py: Bootstrap script (2-3 hours)
     - Test integration: Run workstream with secrets auto-injection (1
   hour)

   proof-of-concept?
